The company said this makes the fund one of its largest shareholders.</p>\n<p>Iyuno-SDI Group was formed after Iyuno Media Group <a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/iyuno-completes-acquisition-of-sdi-media-and-announces-new-company-as-iyuno-sdi-group-301256565.html\">completed its acquisition of SDI Media last month</a>. In a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/17/how-localization-leader-iyuno-media-group-opens-entertainment-to-international-audiences/\">recent interview with TechCrunch</a>, Iyuno-SDI Group chief executive officer David Lee, who launched Iyuno in 2002 while he was an undergraduate in Seoul, described how the company&#8217;s proprietary cloud-based enterprise resource planning software allows it to perform localization services—including subtitles, dubbing and accessibility features—at scale.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"qOFhocHltM\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/17/how-localization-leader-iyuno-media-group-opens-entertainment-to-international-audiences/\">How localization leader Iyuno Media Group opens entertainment to international audiences</a></p></blockquote><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;How localization leader Iyuno Media Group opens entertainment to international audiences&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/17/how-localization-leader-iyuno-media-group-opens-entertainment-to-international-audiences/embed/#?secret=qOFhocHltM\" data-secret=\"qOFhocHltM\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Iyuno also built its own neural machine translation engines, trained on data from specific entertainment genres, to help its human translators work more quickly. The company’s clients have included Netflix, Apple iTunes, DreamWorks, HBO and Entertainment One.</p>\n<p>Now that its merger is complete, Iyuno-SDI Group operates a combined 67 offices in 34 countries, and is able to perform localization services in more than 100 languages.</p>\n<p>SoftBank Group <a href=\"https://www.crunchbase.com/funding_round/iyuno-media-group-series-a--2d6e9d8c\">first invested in Iyuno Media Group through SoftBank Ventures Asia</a>, its venture capital arm, in 2018. SoftBank Vision 2 will join Lee and investors Altor, Shamrock Capital Advisors and SoftBank Ventures Asia Corporation on Iyuno-SDI Group’s board of directors.</p>\n<div class=\"embed 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"Gillmor Gang: Days Go By","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136206","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/8-DEQ96Fsf0?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;fs=1&#038;hl=en-US&#038;autohide=2&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;' sandbox='allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation'></iframe></p>\n<p>You may ask yourself, say the Talking Heads. What is this thing working from anywhere? Or as Google says, work from right here in the office. As the vaccines roll on out, some of us are just not ready for returning to normal. On this edition of the Gillmor Gang, the office is a state of mind, served up by Zoom and Clubhouse. It sounds like Clownhouse, with unlimited fungible bozos on the menu.</p>\n<p>Surely we are binged out, election recalled, floating in a vat of VC alphabet soup. SPACs are everywhere and nowhere, water cooled conversations masquerading as big ticket conferences, right wing looneys seeking blanket pardons. And we&#8217;re applying for permission to stay home in our digital workshops? Yes, it will probably work for a hot second, but when will the research measure what has really changed. After a year of living a nightmare, some of us are ready for anything but the rest of our lives.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The other day on Clubhouse, they celebrated the life and times of Hal Willner, a record producer extraordinaire who died suddenly of COVID at 64. My Gang colleague Michael Markman sent me a Clubhouse notification suggesting I might want to listen in, and I did. I knew Hal a little bit, worked with him on several of his projects, and made the mistake we all make too often of assuming he or she would be around for the duration. So I clicked on the link and found myself in a room full of people who knew him a whole lot better. It was cathartic to hear them try and describe the guy, his life&#8217;s work, his day job at Saturday Night Live, and his magical series of projects pairing the strangest combinations of artists you could not even imagine. But he did.</p>\n<p>So when we start to figure out this new world we&#8217;ve been propelled into, the normal we are fashioning out of the hints the virus has left us about what&#8217;s important, we all knew Willner and the mischievous glint in his eye just enough to wish for just a little more help in the now. His friends were on surer footing in this crazy clubhouse, chiming in from literally all over the world. Some saw him as a mentor, others as a collaborator, me with the twinge of regret for not being remotely brave enough to appreciate the brief window into this gentle giant for the luck of the encounter. I knew he was special, I knew it didn&#8217;t matter how or why we all got there at some time, and here was Clubhouse serving up a human experience only possible because people like Hal seized these moments of the days going by.</p>\n<p>Yet it&#8217;s easy to say these new constructs are built like a house of cards, that the hype will fade, the economics atrophy, the big get bigger. It may all be true, but what part of the really big idea Clubhouse or Medium or Substack is truly vulnerable? There is where it becomes political posturing as much as anything. Just because the current or pivoted business model is suspect doesn&#8217;t mean success isn&#8217;t lurking just around the corner. If the world is suddenly toxic, does that preclude the idea that adjusting to the emergency can produce new realities that can improve on the nature of conventional reality?</p>\n<p>Take Medium for a second. The writing platform announced a blogging flashback, blogrolls, as a new feature to amplify signals of affection for favorite authors. The Medium analytics are harnessed to project an organically-updating list of favorite follows informed by recent updates by the authors. For the readers, this is a convenient hybrid of social and feeds; for the writers an incentive to gain timely traction in the community of what on Twitter we call the social cloud. It is simple in execution but deep in purpose, as it encourages you to post to Medium. The platform has recently pivoted away from funding original content after pivoting away from eyeball-driven advertising, but this new feature could be a way of letting the existing architecture fund the growth of strategic analytics. The more you deliver signal to the follow notification stream, the more you prime the pump of handclaps and time to click metrics, which increases the strength of the blogroll signal and so it goes.</p>\n<p>You may ask yourself, what does this have to do with working from anywhere? Well, the idea you can nurture a self-healing community of co-workers through digital technologies is right at the top of the list of things we want to do to bolster the new economy. While audio is seen as subtractive from video, it is additive in terms of broadening the user base beyond so-called creators to the so-called doers, the folks who move the products and services from place to place. It&#8217;s radio, a companion stream of news, music, soap box, ideas, alerts, reminders, and coffee breaks that fuels the day and lights the night. It&#8217;s digital mom and pop.</p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\"><strong><em>from the <a href=\"https://www.getrevue.co/profile/gillmorgang/issues/gillmor-gang-newsletter-revue-5-514665\"> Gillmor Gang Newsletter</a></em></strong></p>\n<p style=\"text-align: center\">__________________</p>\n<p>The Gillmor Gang — Frank Radice, Michael Markman, Keith Teare, Denis Pombriant, Brent Leary and Steve Gillmor. 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"Elior acquires food delivery startup Nestor","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136328","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Corporate catering company <a href=\"https://www.elior.fr\">Elior</a> has acquired French startup <a href=\"https://nestorparis.com\">Nestor</a> for an undisclosed amount. Nestor originally started with a simple idea to differentiate itself from food delivery giants, such as Deliveroo, Uber Eats and others.</p>\n<p>Every day, the startup offered a single menu for lunch. If you liked what was on the menu, you could order and get delivered 10 to 20 minutes later. By offering a single menu, a delivery person could deliver several clients in a single ride. Similarly, by managing its own kitchen, Nestor could improve its margins as it didn’t have to pay third-party restaurants.</p>\n<p>Since I first covered Nestor <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/05/30/nestor-focuses-on-delivering-lunch-for-office-workers-in-paris/\">in 2016</a>, the company has been capital efficient and mostly focused on this unique product offering. Elior says that Nestor managed to reach 10,000 meals per week.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Over the past few months, Nestor has tried to launch new offers. For instance, companies can switch to Nestor for their canteens. The startup delivers meals in fridges directly. It reminds me of <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/11/foodles-raises-another-10-million-for-its-cloud-canteen/\">Foodles</a>, another French startup focused on canteen-like services.</p>\n<p>Nestor can also deliver individually packed lunches in case you are spending the day with some clients for a big meeting. <a href=\"https://popchef.com\">Popchef</a> has also pivoted to focus more on that segment.</p>\n<p>Following the acquisition, Nestor is going to focus more and more on the B2B market. While Elior is working with big companies in glass towers, it has been quite hard to convince small and medium companies to open a canteen in the office.</p>\n<p>The sales pitch could be summed up in two sentences. Nestor clients don’t need to have their own kitchen as everything is prepared in advance. And employees don’t have to browse Deliveroo at lunch time to find something that isn’t a burger or a pizza.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" welcome back to <a href=\"https://open.spotify.com/show/5IEYLip3eDppcOmy5DmphC?si=bjgo57TCQ-uFC38-iTy6HA\">Equity</a>, TechCrunch’s venture capital-focused podcast, where we unpack the numbers behind the headlines.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/nmasc_\">Natasha</a> and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/DannyCrichton\">Danny</a> and  and <a href=\"https://twitter.com/gracedenhall\">Grace</a> were all here to chat through the week’s rigamarole of news. <a href=\"https://twitter.com/alex\">Alex</a> took some well-deserved time off, but that meant we got to poke a little fun at him and create a Special Edition segment to start off the show.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Jokes aside, this week was yet another spree of creator economy, edtech, and new fund announcements, with fresh and unexpected news hailing from Natasha&#8217;s home state, New Jersey.</p>\n<p>Here&#8217;s what we got into:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Box got a lifeline in the form of a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/08/kkr-hands-box-a-500m-lifeline/\">$500 million check from KKR</a>, and as Danny mentions, Box CEO Aaron Levie shifts his role a bit, too.</li>\n<li>Patreon, an early startup in the creator economy space, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/06/patreon-triples-valuation-to-4-billion/\">has tripled its valuation to $4 billion.</a> Another, not-so-old startup with the same reported valuation? Clubhouse. We threaded the line between the two, and gave some color on <a href=\"https://www.google.com/search?q=clubhouse+monetization+techcrunch&#38;rlz=1C5GCEA_enUS901US901&#38;oq=clubhouse+monetization+techcrunch&#38;aqs=chrome..69i57.3826j0j4&#38;sourceid=chrome&#38;ie=UTF-8\">a new monetization feature</a> rolled out.</li>\n<li>As an aside, looks like Clubhouse is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/07/twitter-said-to-have-held-acquisition-talks-with-clubhouse-on-potential-4b-deal/\">everyone&#8217;s favorite app to tweet about</a> so much so that even Twitter is reportedly considering an acquisition.</li>\n<li><a style=\"background-color: #ffffff; font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\" href=\"https://www.axios.com/masterclass-new-funding-25-billion-valuation-f75521cd-3a85-4215-b4fa-c2ae48da9765.html?utm_campaign=organic&#38;utm_medium=socialshare&#38;utm_source=twitter\">MasterClass raising new funding at $2.5 billion valuation.</a> That is up from a $800 million valuation just last year, and shows that aspirational teaching packaged as celebrity-taught Youtube-like videos with Netflix-like quality is enough to be considered edtech.</li>\n<li>Speaking of edtech, a series of exits have caught our attention. <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/01/how-is-edtech-spending-its-extra-capital/\">The consolidation has begun! </a></li>\n<li>We spoke about two new funds. First, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/06/new-jersey-announces-10m-seed-fund-aimed-at-black-and-latinx-founders/\">New Jersey is proposing a $10 million fund</a> that would go to Black and LatinX founders. Second, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/08/index-closes-200-million-dedicated-seed-fund-to-intensify-multi-stage-thesis/\">Index raised nine-figures for seed startups,</a> beating Sequoia&#8217;s seed fund by a measly $5 million.</li>\n<li>The show closed with two early-stage funding rounds you don&#8217;t want to miss &#8211; <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/07/walnut-affirm-for-healthcare-seed/?tpcc=ECTW2020\">Walnut</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/06/real-raises-10m-from-lightspeed-megan-rapinoe-and-others-to-rethink-therapy/\">Real</a> &#8211; as well as a conversation on the future of telehealth.</li>\n</ul>\n<p>What a show! 00:41:36","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:36","title":"6 VCs talk the future of Austin’s exploding startup ecosystem","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2133404","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">For years now, a growing number of tech companies &#8212; large and small &#8212; have either relocated their headquarters to Austin or opened another office or campus in the Texas capital. They&#8217;ve been drawn to the city for a number of factors, including its laid-back lifestyle, no state tax, a business-friendly environment and lower cost of living (for now).</p>\n<p>The impact on the city’s startup ecosystem is noticeable in the growing number of entrepreneurs (many of whom worked at some of the tech giants who have a big presence in the city) and investors calling Austin home.</p>\n<p>Most recently, Tesla’s plans to build a gigafactory in the city and Oracle’s announcement that it was relocating its headquarters here have made national headlines.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The comparisons to the Bay Area abound &#8212; from the burgeoning and maturing startup scene to an overheated and competitive housing market.</p>\n<p>All the while, venture capitalists see several key areas of opportunities. At one point, Austin was once a big enterprise software city. While software is still big here, a number of other sectors are growing including CPG (consumer packaged goods) and real estate tech, among others.</p>\n<p>What follows is a survey of some of the top VCs in the city and their projections about the growth of Austin’s ecosystem.</p>\n<p><strong>Here&#8217;s who we spoke to:</strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>Eric Engineer, S3 Ventures</li>\n<li>Morgan Flager, Silverton Partners</li>\n<li>Joshua Baer, Capital Factory</li>\n<li><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;Answer by Unorthodox Ventures Founding Contrarian Carey Smith\\n\\nWho knows? The problem with prognosticating is there’s never any follow up. “Futurists” spin predictions, and the public consumes them like cotton candy, and no one bothers to check back years later and see how accurate they were. It’s hard enough just to characterize the scene as it is right now. There are so many companies of so many different sizes doing so many different things, and there isn’t really a unifying characteristic beyond growth and innovation. It really could go any direction.&#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">Carey Smith, Unorthodox Ventures</span></li>\n<li>Krishna Srinivasan, LiveOak Venture Partners</li>\n<li> Zaz Floreani,<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\"> Next Coast Ventures</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;Where do you see Austin's startup scene five years from now? The city has attracted a wide range of people over the years, including more big tech and startups very recently. How will it add up to something more than the sum of the parts? &#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\"><strong>Where do you see Austin&#8217;s startup scene five years from now? The city has attracted a wide range of people over the years, including more big tech and startups very recently. How will it add up to something more than the sum of the parts?</strong> </span></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;At S3 Ventures, we like to say that “our thesis is Texas”. We believe that by 2030, the Texas startup ecosystem could be the country’s second largest. \\n\\nTexas has a multi-decade history when it comes to technology innovation. This is not a flash in the pan; it is a long-term trend that is accelerating and just now getting national attention. Tech ecosystems benefit from virtuous cycles: as more talented people move to Texas, more capital will follow them, which will then attract more talent, and so on. &#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">Eric Engineer of S3 Ventures believes that by 2030, the Texas startup ecosystem could be the country’s second largest.</span></p>\n<p>&#8220;Tech ecosystems benefit from virtuous cycles. As more talented people move to Texas, more capital will follow them, which will then attract more talent, and so on,&#8221; he said.</p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;At S3 Ventures, we like to say that “our thesis is Texas”. We believe that by 2030, the Texas startup ecosystem could be the country’s second largest. \\n\\nTexas has a multi-decade history when it comes to technology innovation. This is not a flash in the pan; it is a long-term trend that is accelerating and just now getting national attention. Tech ecosystems benefit from virtuous cycles: as more talented people move to Texas, more capital will follow them, which will then attract more talent, and so on. &#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">Morgan Flager of 16-year-old Silverton Partners says since Silverton&#8217;s inception more than 16 years ago, the state&#8217;s largest VC firm has always bet on Austin and, more broadly, on Texas. </span></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;At S3 Ventures, we like to say that “our thesis is Texas”. This is not a flash in the pan; it is a long-term trend that is accelerating and just now getting national attention. Tech ecosystems benefit from virtuous cycles: as more talented people move to Texas, more capital will follow them, which will then attract more talent, and so on. &#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">&#8220;We’ve always felt that if Austin wins, we win, and that’s how we’ve run our business,&#8221; he says. &#8220;But we are just one organization, and now we are joined by many others who are also betting on Austin and want to do their part to make this ecosystem better&#8230;Moving forward, a critical component of success is fostering this existing philosophy of community collaboration, which has already played a part in making Austin such an attractive place to be. If we continue to hold on to that core philosophy as we grow, we’re in for an amazing future.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;In 5 years from now Austin will have gone from \\&#34;up and coming\\&#34; to \\&#34;arrived,\\&#34; from the top of the Tier 2 cities to a competitive Tier 1 city. Founders need to make sure they are selective about the investors and advisers they take on and that they choose people who offer more than just capital.&#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\"><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">&#8220;Founders need to make sure they are selective about the investors and advisers they take on and that they choose people who offer more than just capital,&#8221; he said.</span><br />\n</span></p>\n<p>LiveOak Ventures&#8217; Srinivasan warns that people in Austin<span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;\\nPeople here are not transactional—and if you come across as being transactional and strictly interact with somebody in a transactional way and not a relational way---it rubs people the wrong way. Outsiders need to be aware of this when they come here. When making a hiring decision, it’s important to choose someone who is a good cultural fit, and not hire based solely on resume. From an investor perspective, if you want to do business here, it’s important to focus building strong relationships, besides offering attractive deal terms.&#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\"> are not transactional and that if you come across as being transactional and strictly interact with somebody in a transactional way and not a relational way, &#8220;it rubs people the wrong way.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;\\nPeople here are not transactional—and if you come across as being transactional and strictly interact with somebody in a transactional way and not a relational way---it rubs people the wrong way. Floreani notes that hiring growth leaders has been a consistent challenge across her firm&#8217;s portfolio. &#8220;It would be great if Austin had a deeper bench of talented marketing and sales leaders,&#8221; she said.</span></p>\n<p><strong>Who are key startup people you see creating success locally, whether investors, founders or even other types of startup ecosystems roles like lawyers, designers, growth experts, etc. We’re trying to highlight the movers and shakers who outsiders might not know.</strong></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;Founders/CEOs – Leo Resig (Atmosphere), Jag Bath (Favor), Kim Rodriguez (Acessa), Doug Donovan (Interplay Learning), Richard Lebovitz (LeanDNA), Adelle Archer (Eterneva), Andy Ambrose (LiveOak Technology), Adam Berman (TVA Medical), Dion Cornett (Liquibase) \\n\\nInvestors - Rosa McCormick (Wild Basin), Oksana Malysheva (Sputnik), Adam Lipman (Ecliptic Capital), and Josh Baer / Bryan Chambers (Capital Factory) \\n\\nService Providers – Marc Nathan (E/N), John Gump (CBRE), Lathrop Smith (MLR), Austin Willis (SVB), Paul O’Brien (Mediatech) &#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\"><strong>S3:</strong> Founders/CEOs – Leo Resig (Atmosphere), Jag Bath (Favor), Kim Rodriguez (Acessa), Doug Donovan (Interplay Learning), Richard Lebovitz (LeanDNA), Adelle Archer (Eterneva), Andy Ambrose (LiveOak Technology), Adam Berman (TVA Medical), Dion Cornett (Liquibase)</span></p>\n<p>Investors &#8211; Please note I may be a bit biased here as most of these are companies we have backed.</span></p>\n<p><strong>What do you think of comparisons to Silicon Valley? What impact do you think the influx of (big &#38; small) tech companies is having on the city&#8217;s startup scene?</strong></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;There is only one Silicon Valley, and it is highly unlikely there will be anything comparable in the Western world. \\n\\nWhile much smaller today, if the trends continue over the next ten years, the Texas ecosystem has a real shot at growing as large, if not larger, than NY and Boston. &#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">S3&#8217;s Engineer believes there is only one Silicon Valley, and that it is highly unlikely there will be anything comparable in the Western world.</span></p>\n<p>But he thinks that while much smaller today, if the trends continue over the next ten years, the Texas ecosystem has a real shot at growing as large, if not larger, than New York and Boston.</p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;I was born and raised in Silicon Valley. I went to school out there and worked there as well. With that said, I’m not a big fan of the comparison. Each place is distinct with different pro’s and con’s. Will Austin ever overtake Silicon Valley in terms of size and activity? I really don’t know -- we certainly have a long way to go. To some extent, I’m not sure that matters.\\n\\nWhat I do care about is that Austin retains its vibrant character and that our current growth enriches the city, rather than dilutes its energy. It’s important to recognize that Austin’s culture has not been tech-centric. Austin is a unique powerhouse of live music, great food, arts, outdoor living and “keeping it weird”.\\n\\nAs I contemplate what I admire about Silicon Valley and all the things Austin needs to do to be at that level, I tend to spend as much time thinking about what we could do differently.&#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">Silverton&#8217;s Flager was born and raised in Silicon Valley. He went to school there and worked there as well. As a result, he&#8217;s not a big fan of the comparison. </span></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;I was born and raised in Silicon Valley. Will Austin ever overtake Silicon Valley in terms of size and activity? I really don’t know -- we certainly have a long way to go. To some extent, I’m not sure that matters.\\n\\nWhat I do care about is that Austin retains its vibrant character and that our current growth enriches the city, rather than dilutes its energy. It’s important to recognize that Austin’s culture has not been tech-centric. Austin is a unique powerhouse of live music, great food, arts, outdoor living and “keeping it weird”.\\n\\nAs I contemplate what I admire about Silicon Valley and all the things Austin needs to do to be at that level, I tend to spend as much time thinking about what we could do differently.&#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">&#8220;Each place is distinct with different pros and cons,&#8221; he said. &#8220;Will Austin ever overtake Silicon Valley in terms of size and activity? I really don’t know &#8212; we certainly have a long way to go. To some extent, I’m not sure that matters.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>What he does care about is that Austin retains its vibrant character and that its current growth enriches the city, rather than dilutes its energy. &#8220;It’s important to recognize that Austin’s culture has not been tech-centric,&#8221; Flager said. &#8220;Austin is a unique powerhouse of live music, great food, arts, outdoor living and &#8216;keeping it weird.&#8217; &#8221;</p>\n<p>He adds: &#8220;As I contemplate what I admire about Silicon Valley and all the things Austin needs to do to be at that level, I tend to spend as much time thinking about what we could do differently.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Unorthodox Ventures&#8217; Smith believes it&#8217;s no surprise that &#8220;<span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;Answer by Unorthodox Ventures Founding Contrarian Carey Smith\\n\\nOf course everyone wants to leave Silicon Valley — they finally figured out it’s a disaster. As more intelligent, hardworking and curious people gather here, it’s a good thing for Austin and for VCs more broadly. One of the problems with Silicon Valley is that such a strong percentage of VC money stays there or in New York or Boston. We need more capital in Austin and other innovative cities throughout Middle America where we’re solving real problems for the everyday American. As Austin feels more and more influence from Silicon Valley, it’s so important to fund more than tech-oriented projects. Venture capitalists need to focus on basic human needs, too.&#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">everyone wants to leave Silicon Valley.</span></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;Answer by Unorthodox Ventures Founding Contrarian Carey Smith\\n\\nOf course everyone wants to leave Silicon Valley — they finally figured out it’s a disaster. As Austin feels more and more influence from Silicon Valley, it’s so important to fund more than tech-oriented projects. Venture capitalists need to focus on basic human needs, too.&#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">&#8220;They finally figured out it’s a disaster,&#8221; he said. &#8220;As more intelligent, hardworking and curious people gather here, it’s a good thing for Austin and for VCs more broadly. As Austin feels more and more influence from Silicon Valley, it’s so important to fund more than tech-oriented projects. Venture capitalists need to focus on basic human needs, too.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p>LiveOak&#8217;s Srinivasan knows that c<span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;Comparisons to Silicon Valley are inevitable, and for the most part welcome, insomuch as those comparisons bring broader national and international attention to Austin and reinforces our reputation as a city with a booming startup scene. There’s a lot of vibrancy and momentum to the startup scene here that is reminiscent of the early days of Silicon Valley--the growing number businesses being launched, the number of companies being funded, the amount of talent flowing here eager to engrain themselves in the tech community. Yet we know there is something unique to Austin that sets it apart from any other tech hub—the collaborative spirit of the people here. There’s also an energy and excitement in this community that’s palpable. Austin has great respect for the successes Silicon Valley has brought forth, and we will incorporate their positive aspects, while forging our own path.\\n \\nThe influx of big and small tech companies is bringing more experienced tech workers who, over time, will spin out of those companies and start new businesses. This should lead to more business growth and more startup activity. Most likely, this influx will bring leaders who are experienced in scaling large companies and who can leverage that experience to launch the next big company in Austin with higher aspirations for even larger outcomes.&#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">omparisons to Silicon Valley are inevitable, and for the most part welcome when those comparisons bring broader national and international attention to Austin and reinforces its reputation as a city with a booming startup scene. </span></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;Comparisons to Silicon Valley are inevitable, and for the most part welcome, insomuch as those comparisons bring broader national and international attention to Austin and reinforces our reputation as a city with a booming startup scene. There’s also an energy and excitement in this community that’s palpable. Austin has great respect for the successes Silicon Valley has brought forth, and we will incorporate their positive aspects, while forging our own path.&#8221;</span></p>\n<p><span data-sheets-value=\"{&#34;1&#34;:2,&#34;2&#34;:&#34;Comparisons to Silicon Valley are inevitable, and for the most part welcome, insomuch as those comparisons bring broader national and international attention to Austin and reinforces our reputation as a city with a booming startup scene. There’s also an energy and excitement in this community that’s palpable. Austin has great respect for the successes Silicon Valley has brought forth, and we will incorporate their positive aspects, while forging our own path.\\n \\nThe influx of big and small tech companies is bringing more experienced tech workers who, over time, will spin out of those companies and start new businesses. This should lead to more business growth and more startup activity. Most likely, this influx will bring leaders who are experienced in scaling large companies and who can leverage that experience to launch the next big company in Austin with higher aspirations for even larger outcomes.&#34;}\" data-sheets-userformat=\"{&#34;2&#34;:513,&#34;3&#34;:{&#34;1&#34;:0},&#34;12&#34;:0}\">Next Coast&#8217;s Floreani believes that comparison has been overused for a decade. &#8220;We are not Silicon Valley and will never be it,&#8221; she says. &#8220;I am not saying that in a negative sense. I simply believe we grow companies differently here and even though more SV talent and investors are coming to town I don&#8217;t think we will suddenly shift to a more Valley like approach to growing companies like blitz-scaling. 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"So you want to raise a Series A","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2134119","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">During a seed funding round, a founder needs to convince a venture capital investor on a vision. But during a Series A fundraise, napkin-stage ideas don’t make the cut — a founder needs product progress, numbers, and revenue (or at least a plan to eventually generate some).</p>\n<p>In many ways, the stakes are higher for a Series A — and Bucky Moore, a partner at Kleiner Perkins, joined <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/tag/early-stage-2021/\">TechCrunch Early Stage</a> last week to give founders tactical advice on the process of raising one.</p>\n<p>Moore spoke about storytelling over semantics, pricing, and where his firm sees itself “raising the bar” for startups.</p>\n<p>Here are a few key points; a full video and a transcript of the entire conversation are linked at the bottom.</p>\n<hr />\n<h2>Explain to investors why you are raising now</h2>\n<p>More companies will raise seed rounds than Series A rounds, simply due to the fact that many startups fail, and venture only makes sense for a small fraction of businesses out there. Every check is a new cycle of convincing and proving that you, as a startup, will have venture-scale returns. Moore explained that startups looking to move to their next round need to explain to investors why now is their moment.</p>\n<blockquote><p>The way I think about “why now” is [that] it is an opportunity for you as a founder to convey a unique insight and understanding of your market opportunity, the history of the space that you&#8217;re in, why companies have succeeded or failed in that space, historically speaking, and what are the known challenges from a go-to-market perspective; what headwinds will you be up against at a macro level. These are all things that I think people like me get really excited about when hearing unique insight from founders, because it suggests that they&#8217;ve really studied their market opportunity, and they understand it. <strong><em>(Timestamp: 2:19)</em></strong></p></blockquote>\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/03/11-words-and-phrases-to-cut-from-your-vc-pitch-deck/\">11 words and phrases to cut from your VC pitch deck</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/11/as-covid-19-era-drags-on-vcs-look-beyond-zoom-calls-for-due-diligence-and-sourcing/\">As COVID-19 era drags on, VCs look beyond Zoom calls for due diligence and sourcing</a></li>\n</ul>\n<p><div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=IQEmOoWj6WA:3UEJjDWUX5I:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"Amazon defeats warehouse union push, RWDSU challenges results","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136403","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Efforts to unionize Amazon’s Bessemer, Alabama warehouse were defeated by a wide margin in the second day of vote counting. More than half of the 3,215 votes cast broke in in factor of the retailer. The Retail, Wholesale and Department Store Union, which would have served as the workers&#8217; union, had the vote passed, was quick to challenge the results.</p>\n<p>RWDSU President Stuart Appelbaum said in a statement offered to TechCrunch,</p>\n<blockquote><p>Amazon has left no stone unturned in its efforts to gaslight its own employees. We won’t let Amazon’s lies, deception and illegal activities go unchallenged, which is why we are formally filing charges against all of the egregious and blatantly illegal actions taken by Amazon during the union vote. Amazon knew full well that unless they did everything they possibly could, even illegal activity, their workers would have continued supporting the union.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>That’s why they required all their employees to attend lecture after lecture, filled with mistruths and lies, where workers had to listen to the company demand they oppose the union. That’s why they flooded the internet, the airwaves and social media with ads spreading misinformation. That’s why they brought in dozens of outsiders and union-busters to walk the floor of the warehouse. That’s why they bombarded people with signs throughout the facility and with text messages and calls at home. And that’s why they have been lying about union dues in a right to work state. Amazon’s conduct has been despicable.</p></blockquote>\n<p>This initial defeat represents a large setback in the biggest unionization push in Amazon’s 27 year history. What might have represented a sea change for both the retail giant and blue collar tech workers has, for now, been fairly soundly defeated.</p>\n<p>Amazon has, of course, long insisted that it treats workers fairly, making such union efforts unnecessary. The company cites such standards as a $15 an hour minimum wage, a factor the company initial pushed back on, but ultimately instated after pressure from legislators.</p>\n<p>It was a hard fought battle on both sides. A number of legislators threw their weight behind unionization efforts, in an unlikely alliance that ranged from Bernie Sanders to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/12/marco-rubio-says-he-stands-with-amazon-warehouse-workers/\">Marco Rubio</a>. The conservative Florida Senator noted the company&#8217;s “uniquely malicious corporate behavior.” President Joe Biden also sided with the workers, calling himself, “the most pro-union president you’ve ever seen.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The company will no doubt tout the results as vindication. It noted in an early statement, &#8220;[O]ur employees are smart and know the truth—starting wages of $15 or more, health care from day one, and a safe and inclusive workplace. We encourage all of our employees to vote.” We&#8217;ve reached out to the company for a statement following this morning&#8217;s news.</p>\n<p>Among the expected challenges from the union are lingering questions around ballot boxes reportedly installed by the company in violation of labor board terms.&#8221;[E]ven though the NLRB definitively denied Amazon&#8217;s request for a drop box on the warehouse property, Amazon felt it was above the law and worked with the postal service anyway to install one,&#8221; the RWDSU writes. &#8220;They did this because it provided a clear ability to intimidate workers.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The Bessemer warehouse, which employees around 6,000 workers, was opened at the end of March 2020, as the company looked to expand the operation of its essential workers during the impending lock down. The conversation has surface variously long standing complaints around the company&#8217;s treatment of blue collar workers, including numerous reports that employees urinate in water bottles, in order to meet stringent performance standards.</p>\n<p>The company initially denied these claims during a social media offensive, but later clarified its stance in an apology of sorts, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/03/amazon-addresses-pee-bottle-denial-tweet/\">appearing to shift the blame</a> to wider industry problems. The company also ran anti-union ads on its subsidiary, Twitch, before the streaming platform pulled them, stating that they &#8220;should never have been allowed to run.&#8221;</p>\n<p>All told, 3,215 were cast, representing more than half of the workers at the Alabama warehouse. In spite of Amazon winning more than half the votes, counting will continue. Challenges are likely to stretch on for weeks.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"qgjL4q7Nla\"><p><a +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"86f0d76ed2e1603aae8701bac2c22cd8","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn35@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-41-36-205_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Brian Heater","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn35@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-41-36-205_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn47@2020_5/2021/04/09/16-42-25-878_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn4@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-25-351_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=yeB3ptpiZzg:7e3BKd63eME:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn78@2020_2/2021/04/09/16-42-25-331_5d718053e6ee8afd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=yeB3ptpiZzg:7e3BKd63eME:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn84@2020_4/2021/04/09/16-42-25-927_83351230b6862532.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn67@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-42-25-759_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/yeB3ptpiZzg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn83@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-25-472_7056e2528a65ea39.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617986495985},{"createdTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"The 2022 Chevrolet Bolt EUV lowers the cost of entry for some of GM’s most advanced tech","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2133429","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The 2022 Chevy Bolt EUV may look like a larger, slightly longer Chevrolet Bolt, but under that boxy exterior lies a whole lot of tech that&#8217;s both affordable and very advanced. With the launch of the Chevy Bolt EUV, and its available suite of advanced driver assistance systems, GM is putting both advanced driver assistance technology and electric drivetrains within reach of the masses.</p>\n<p>As part of GMs much-touted goal to introduce 30 new electric vehicles in the next four years, the company recently launched an updated Bolt, as well as the all-new Bolt EUV, or Electric Utility Vehicle. I had two separate opportunities to test prototypes of the Bolt EUV with GM&#8217;s advanced Super Cruise system.</p>\n<p>While the Bolt and Bolt EUV share similar DNA, they are two different vehicles. The EUV is the longer and larger of the two, with more bells and whistles, like Super Cruise: An advanced driver assistance system that allows for hands-free driving on certain highways, available as a $2,200 option. Super Cruise is not available on the 2022 Bolt.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<h2>Nuts and bolts</h2>\n<p>The Bolt EUV is powered by a 288-cell, 65-kWh battery pack that Chevy says makes 200 hp and 266 lb-ft of torque. Chevrolet estimates that the EUV will get 250 miles on a full charge, and when charging on the go, can regain up to 95 miles of range in 30 minutes on a Level 2 charger.</p>\n<p>On household power, (specifically 240V) the EUV will take around 7-8 hours to charge up to 100%, which is how Chevy says it expects most consumers will power their crossover. To assist with that, Chevrolet had teamed up with home charging installer Qmerit to offer free charger installation if you buy or lease a new Bolt or EUV. Installation of a home charger can cost as much as $2,000, so it&#8217;s a decent incentive.</p>\n<p>The Bolt EUV won&#8217;t get the upgraded Ultium battery pack and underlying architecture that&#8217;s coming on the Hummer EV, Cadillac Lyric and other future GM electric vehicles. Instead, the Bolt EUV is built on the BEV2 architecture, the same one on which the 2021 Bolt is built. As mentioned, it also gets Super Cruise as an optional add-on.</p>\n<p>Since Super Cruise&#8217;s introduction in 2017, the system has been siloed in Cadillac products, showing up on the 2018 CT6 and finally expanding to the 2021 CT5. The Bolt EUV is the first production vehicle outside of a luxury GM brand to offer the system even as paid upgrade.</p>\n<p>The Bolt EUV starts at $33,995, which is $2,500 less than the 2021 Bolt that is sitting on dealer lots today. The 2022 Chevy Bolt ($31,995) is also around $4,500 cheaper than the 2021 Bolt. Chevy&#8217;s press department says that the goal is to &#8220;make EVs attainable to everyone.&#8221; Although this is also likely an effort to bring the new vehicles in line with earlier Bolt models that qualified for the $7,500 federal tax credit. That incentive in the U.S. disappeared after GM sold 200,000 EVs nationwide.</p>\n<p>The Launch Edition, which included the optional Super Cruise, a lighted charging port and special badging, carried a sticker price of $43,495. As of this writing, reservations for the Launch Edition are completely full, but you can still reserve an LT or Premier trim in the 2022 Bolt EUV. Super Cruise, however, is only available as a $2,200 option on the Premier trim, which starts at $38,495. Keep in mind, these prices are all before including any state or local tax incentives or rebates for electric vehicles.</p>\n<p>In contrast, a Tesla Model Y Long Range model, the most affordable of the bunch since Tesla dropped that vehicle&#8217;s base option, starts at $41,990 before incentives. Getting Tesla&#8217;s so called Full-Self Driving feature — which is not self-driving and is actually a driver assistance system — will cost you an additional $10,000.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"DGvqcsFSbI\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/02/24/can-solid-state-batteries-power-up-for-the-next-generation-of-evs/\">Can solid state batteries power up for the next generation of EVs?</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Can solid state batteries power up for the next generation of EVs?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/02/24/can-solid-state-batteries-power-up-for-the-next-generation-of-evs/embed/#?secret=DGvqcsFSbI\" data-secret=\"DGvqcsFSbI\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<h2>User experience: Super Cruise</h2>\n<p>Super Cruise, while impressive, tends to err on the side of caution when it comes to implementing the technology. The system allows for drivers to take their hands and feet off the controls on more than 200,000 miles of mapped divided highway all over the country.</p>\n<p>&#8220;If we can bring congestion and crashes to zero, then developing fully-autonomous driving is worth it,&#8221; Jeremy Short, the vehicle chief engineer who is responsible for the engineering, development, validation, testing and manufacturing of the Bolt EUV, said during my second time with the crossover. &#8220;The next 10 years are going to get really interesting in the autonomy space. Five years ago, would you have thought we would have what we have now with Super Cruise?&#8221;</p>\n<p>That being said, Super Cruise isn&#8217;t perfect, and GM continues to iterate the product, even on the Bolt EUV. During my first drive in a Bolt EUV prototype from Marina Del Rey to Burbank and back in peak Los Angeles rush hour traffic, Super Cruise seemed a little bit &#8220;off.&#8221; The system ping-ponged in the wide lanes on the highway. When the vehicle was moving under 30 mph, the system lost track of the lane markings on mapped highways like the extremely busy 405, causing it to drift toward the other lanes and switch off a number of times.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2136083\" style=\"width: 1290px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2136083\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"breakout wp-image-2136083 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg\" alt=\"2022 Chevrolet Bolt EUV\" width=\"1280\" height=\"970\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg 1280w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg?resize=150,114 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg?resize=300,227 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg?resize=768,582 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg?resize=680,515 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1280px) 100vw, 1280px\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2136083\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">2022 Chevrolet Bolt EUV. <strong>Image Credits:</strong> GM</p></div></p>\n<p>A few weeks later, on a second prototype drive that followed a 50-mile loop originating in Carson, the system appeared to have gained its sea legs. However, both Short, who was following in another prototype vehicle, and I noted that Super Cruise in the EUV still had problems when traffic slowed below 10 mph. When cars ahead slowed, the EUV would slow appropriately, but then begin to drift across the lane once traffic moved forward, as if it had lost the lane markings. Eventually, the alert to take over would sound and Super Cruise would shut off.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I did notice some ping-ponging at low speeds,&#8221; Short said after our drive. He then joked that it will require some more engineers driving that stretch of road to teach the system to navigate it without bouncing around the lane. He also said that speed and California&#8217;s strange concrete roadbeds (they have textured surfaces that can look like lane markings to AI) can affect Super Cruise. &#8220;Think of it like tracer fire; the more data you have coming in, the more accurate the car can be.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Short says that the Super Cruise system is continually learning and updating &#8212; even if it&#8217;s fully baked on vehicles like the CT5 and CT6. Every time Super Cruise is added to a new vehicle, the sensors, software and processing needs to be updated and tweaked because each car has different weights, potential speeds, dimensions, steering and braking, space for sensors and features. For example, you will be able to get a version of Super Cruise on the 2022 Cadillac Escalade which includes automatic lane changing features. The 2022 Bolt EUV, however, doesn&#8217;t get those sensors and therefore can&#8217;t automatically change lanes.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Each vehicle that has Super Cruise implemented has different anatomy so it needs to process and do different things,&#8221; Short said. &#8220;The Super Cruise on the Bolt EUV was developed at the same time that engineers were developing it on the Escalade. There&#8217;s very different steering and braking in each car so the two systems are different.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Super Cruise qualifies as an advanced Level 2 autonomous vehicle. As the driver, you still have to remain alert, and attentive, but you can remove your hands from the steering wheel and your feet from the pedals on roads where Super Cruise is available. Sensors embedded in the steering wheel track your eyes (even at night or when you&#8217;re wearing dark sunglasses) to ensure that you are paying attention to the road ahead and not watching a movie, napping or glancing at your phone. The system doesn&#8217;t give you much leeway to take your eyes off the road while using Super Cruise, either. At 65 mph, you can reach over and change the radio station on the 10.2-inch infotainment screen but alarms will sound if you look away for more than just a few seconds.</p>\n<p>&#8220;If you were on a long drive from Los Angeles to Las Vegas,&#8221; Short explained after I asked about it, &#8220;you&#8217;d essentially be a front passenger. Both you and your passenger would be looking down the road, keeping your eyes up for any potential issues. When I did that trip with a friend and used Super Cruise, I felt the same level of fatigue that he did, which is to say, not much.&#8221;</p>\n<h2>The other bells and whistles</h2>\n<p>We haven&#8217;t had the typical full week to test the 2022 Bolt EUV to fully evaluate. However, there was enough time to evaluate some of the vehicle&#8217;s features.</p>\n<p>Chevy&#8217;s new onboard infotainment and navigation system runs on the company&#8217;s Infotainment 3 software. The system&#8217;s voice control, which has natural language processing, allowed me to do a quick search to find local charging stations.</p>\n<p>The drawback? The system brought up a number of charging stations, but didn&#8217;t indicate which ones were available, in service, out of service, or if they were part of the EvGo system, the charging company that GM has partnered with. Driver&#8217;s also can&#8217;t page through results while using Super Cruise because the driver monitoring system will notice that their eyes aren&#8217;t on the road ahead.</p>\n<p>In order to find EvGo chargers, owners need to use the myChevrolet App to locate the chargers and then send the directions to the navigation system. While driving, the system does lock out some features, and Short notes that you won&#8217;t be able to flip through pages of apps.</p>\n<p>It will be interesting to see how this plays out once we get more time in the EUV. That being said, it&#8217;s not likely to be as seamless as the Tesla charging experience.</p>\n<p>At its core, the 2022 Chevrolet Bolt EUV offers some of the most advanced driver assistance technology on the market in an EV package for an attainable price. After spending two separate four-hour stints in prototype versions of the EUV, it&#8217;s clear that this compact SUV has the space, power and high-tech capability that will allow it to go head-to-head with the likes of the Tesla Model Y, Volvo&#8217;s XC40 Recharge, Ford&#8217;s Mach-E and Volkswagen&#8217;s ID.4.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/OjGFxlC78Eo\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 09 Apr 2021 14:35:43 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg","linkMd5":"338ba4055b230718bfcb286c38c8c91f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn21@2020_5/2021/04/09/16-41-36-839_9aabf6dac1adda50.webp","destWidth":1280,"destHeight":970,"sourceBytes":257374,"destBytes":99252,"author":"Abigail Bassett","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/2022-Chevrolet-BoltEUV-017.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn21@2020_5/2021/04/09/16-41-36-839_9aabf6dac1adda50.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn35@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-41-36-205_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn47@2020_5/2021/04/09/16-42-25-878_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn4@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-25-351_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=OjGFxlC78Eo:v5Zt6Bon0gE:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx31/cdn71@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-42-25-297_fa97ae2f1a7c61db.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=OjGFxlC78Eo:v5Zt6Bon0gE:D7DqB2pKExk":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn67@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-42-25-759_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/OjGFxlC78Eo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn41@2020_2/2021/04/09/16-42-25-466_687bf0601e3dd608.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617986495991},{"createdTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"SnackMagic picks up $15M to expand from build-your-own snack boxes into a wider gifting marketplace","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136309","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">The office shut-down at the start of the Covid-19 pandemic last year spurred huge investment in digital transformation and a wave of tech companies helping with that, but there were some distinct losers in the shift, too &#8212; specifically those whose business models were predicated on serving the very offices that disappeared overnight. Today, one of the companies that had to make an immediate pivot to keep itself afloat is announcing a round of funding, after finding itself not just growing at a clip, but making a profit, as well.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.snackmagic.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">SnackMagic</a>, a build-your-own snack box service, has raised $15 million in a Series A round of funding led by Craft Ventures, with Luxor Capital also participating.</p>\n<p>(Both investors have an interesting track record in the food-on-demand space: Most recently, Luxor co-led a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/31/spains-glovo-picks-up-528m-as-the-food-deliver-market-continues-to-heat-up/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">$528 million round in Glovo in Spain</a>, while Craft backs/has backed the likes of Cloud Kitchens, Postmates and <a href=\"https://www.craftventures.com/portfolio\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">many more</a>).</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The funding comes on the back of a strong year for the company, which hit a $20 million revenue run rate in eight months and turned profitable in December 2020.</p>\n<p>Founder and CEO Shaunak Amin said in an interview that the plan will be to use the funding both to continue growing SnackMagic&#8217;s existing business, as well as extend into other kinds of gifting categories. Currently, you can ship snacks anywhere in the world, but the customizable boxes &#8212; recipients are gifted an amount that they can spend, and they choose what they want in the box themselves from <a href=\"https://www.snackmagic.com/menu/featured\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">SnackMagic&#8217;s menu</a>, or one that a business has created and branded as a subset of that &#8212; are only available in locations in North America, serviced by SnackMagic&#8217;s primary warehouse. Other locations are given options of pre-packed boxes of snacks right now, but the plan is to slowly extend its pick-and-mix model to more geographies, starting with the U.K.</p>\n<p>Alongside this, the company plans to continue widening the categories of items that people can gift each other beyond chocolates, chips, hot sauces and other fun food items, into areas like alcohol, meal kits, and non-food items.&#160;There&#8217;s also scope for expanding to more use cases into areas like corporate gifting, marketing and consumer services, and analytics coming out of its sales.</p>\n<p>Amin calls the data that SnackMagic is amassing about customer interest in different brands and products &#8220;the hidden gem&#8221; of the platform.</p>\n<p>&#8220;It&#8217;s one of the most interesting things,&#8221; he said. Brands that want to add their items to the wider pool of products &#8212; which today numbers between 700 and 800 items &#8212; also get access to a dashboard where they monitor what&#8217;s selling, how much stock is left of their own items, and so on. &#8220;One thing that is very opaque [in the CPG world] is good data.&#8221;</p>\n<p>For many of the bigger companies that lack their own direct sales channels, it&#8217;s a significantly richer data set than what they typically get from selling items in the average brick and mortar store, or from a bigger online retailer like Amazon. &#8220;All these bigger brands like Pepsi and Kellogg not only want to know this about their own products more but also about the brands they are trying to buy,&#8221; Amin said. Several of them, he added, have approached his company to partner and invest, so I guess we should watch this space.</p>\n<p>SnackMagic&#8217;s success comes from a somewhat unintended, unlikely beginning, and it&#8217;s a testament to the power of compelling, yet extensible technology that can be scaled and repurposed if necessary. In its case, there is personalization technology, logistics management, product inventory and accounting, and lots of data analytics involved.</p>\n<p>The company started out as Stadium, a lunch delivery service in New York City that was leveraging the fact that when co-workers ordered lunch or dinner together for the office &#8212; say around a team-building event or a late-night working session, or just for a regular work day &#8212; oftentimes they found that people all hankered for different things to eat.</p>\n<p>In many cases, people typically make separate orders for the different items, but that also means if you are ordering to all eat together, things would not arrive at the same time; if it&#8217;s being expensed, it&#8217;s more complicated on that front too; and if you&#8217;re thinking about carbon footprints, it might also mean a lot less efficiency on that front too.</p>\n<p>Stadium&#8217;s solution was a platform that provided access to multiple restaurants&#8217; menus, and people could pick from all of them for a single order.&#160;The business had been operating for six years and was really starting to take off.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We were quite well known in the city, and we had plans to expand, and we were on track for March 2020 being our best month ever,&#8221; Amin said. Then, Covid-19 hit. &#8220;There was no one left in the office,&#8221; he said. Revenue disappeared overnight, since the idea of delivering many items to one place instantly stopped being a need.</p>\n<p>Amin said that they took a look at the platform they had built to pick many options (and many different costs, and the accounting that came with that) and thought about how to use that for a different end. It turned out that even with people working remotely, companies wanted to give props to their workers, either just to say hello and thanks, or around a specific team event, in the form of food and treats &#8212; all the more so since the supply of snacks you typically come across in so many office canteens and kitchens were no longer there for workers to tap.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s interesting, but perhaps also unsurprising, that one of the by-products of our new way of working has been the rise of more services that cater (no pun intended) to people working in more decentralised ways, and that companies exploring how to improve rewarding people in those environments are also seeing a bump.</p>\n<p>Just yesterday, we wrote about a company called <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/04/08/alyce-an-ai-based-personalised-corporate-gifting-startup-raises-30m/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Alyce raising $30 million for its corporate gifting platform</a> that is also based on personalization &#8212; using AI to help understand the interests of the recipient to make better choices of items that a person might want to receive.</p>\n<p>Alyce is taking a somewhat different approach to SnackMagic: it&#8217;s not holding any products itself, and there is no warehouse but rather a platform that links up buyers with those providing products. And Alyce&#8217;s initial audience is different, too: instead of internal employees (the first, but not final, focus for SnackMagic) it is targeting corporate gifting, or presents that sales and marketing people might send to prospects or current clients as a please and thank you gesture.</p>\n<p>But you can also see how and where the two might meet in the middle &#8212; and compete not just with each other, but the many other online retailers, Amazon and otherwise, plus the consumer goods companies themselves looking for ways of diversifying business by extending beyond the B2C channel.</p>\n<p>&#8220;We don’t worry about Amazon. We just get better,&#8221; Amin said when I asked him about whether he worried that SnackMagic was too easy to replicate. &#8220;It might be tough anyway,&#8221; he added, since &#8220;others might have the snacks but picking and packing and doing individual customization is very different from regular e-commerce. It&#8217;s really more like scalable gifting.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Investors are impressed with the quick turnaround and identification of a market opportunity, and how it quickly retooled its tech to make it fit for purpose.</p>\n<p>“SnackMagic’s immediate success was due to an excellent combination of timing, innovative thinking and world-class execution,” said Bryan Rosenblatt, principal investor at Craft Ventures, in a statement. “As companies embrace the future of a flexible workplace, SnackMagic is not just a snack box delivery platform but a company culture builder.”</p>\n<div +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Dk-_nQ.png?w=680","linkMd5":"d04ce914c1dbe2c705f42fdcef4a2b2e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn5@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-41-45-544_4749a47268849dcf.webp","destWidth":680,"destHeight":191,"sourceBytes":19136,"destBytes":19136,"author":"Anthony Ha","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/01/Dk-_nQ.png?w=680":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn5@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-41-45-544_4749a47268849dcf.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn35@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-41-36-205_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn47@2020_5/2021/04/09/16-42-25-878_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn4@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-25-351_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=B0j54U7sKnY:IaM3INLCs3Y:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn85@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-25-502_2d3cc701f34cc278.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=B0j54U7sKnY:IaM3INLCs3Y:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn12@2020_6/2021/04/09/16-42-25-966_52e7b51148628ba4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn67@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-42-25-759_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/B0j54U7sKnY":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn63@2020_5/2021/04/09/16-42-25-447_1c38133e11a6da2b.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617986496012},{"createdTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"Facebook takes down 16,000 groups trading fake reviews after another poke by UK’s CMA","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136385","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Facebook has removed 16,000 groups that were trading fake reviews on its platform after another intervention by the UK&#8217;s Competition and Markets Authority (CMA), the regulator <a href=\"https://www.gov.uk/government/news/cma-intervention-leads-to-further-facebook-action-on-fake-reviews\">said today</a>.</p>\n<p>The CMA has been leaning on tech giants to prevent their platforms being used as thriving marketplaces for selling fake reviews since it began investigating the issue in 2018 &#8212; <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/21/ebay-and-facebook-told-to-tackle-trade-in-fake-reviews/\">pressuring both eBay and Facebook</a> to act against fake review sellers back in 2019.</p>\n<p>The two companies pledged to do more to tackle the insidious trade <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/08/facebook-and-ebay-pledge-to-do-more-to-tackle-trade-in-fake-reviews-after-pressure-from-uk-regulator/\">last year</a>, after coming under further pressure from the regulator &#8212; which found that Facebook-owned Instagram was also a thriving hub of fake review trades.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"RKEZTgIZqm\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/06/facebook-still-full-of-groups-trading-fake-reviews-says-consumer-group/\">Facebook still full of groups trading fake reviews, says consumer group</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook still full of groups trading fake reviews, says consumer group&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/06/facebook-still-full-of-groups-trading-fake-reviews-says-consumer-group/embed/#?secret=RKEZTgIZqm\" data-secret=\"RKEZTgIZqm\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>The latest intervention by the CMA looks considerably more substantial than last year&#8217;s action &#8212; when Facebook removed a mere 188 groups and disabled 24 user accounts. Although it&#8217;s not clear how many accounts the tech giant has banned and/or suspended this time it has removed orders of magnitude more groups. (We&#8217;ve asked.)</p>\n<p><strong>Update:</strong> We understand that the regulator has focused on the removal of groups trading misleading/fake reviews, rather than individual accounts &#8212; as banned or suspended users are able to create new profiles, whereas removing the group in which fake reviews are being traded is seen as a more effective way to impact and deter the activity.</p>\n<p>Facebook was also contacted with questions but it did not answer what we asked directly, sending us this statement instead:</p>\n<blockquote><p>“We have engaged extensively with the CMA to address this issue. Fraudulent and deceptive activity is not allowed on our platforms, including offering or trading fake reviews. Our safety and security teams are continually working to help prevent these practices.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>Since the CMA has been raising the issue of fake review trading, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/08/06/facebook-still-full-of-groups-trading-fake-reviews-says-consumer-group/\">Facebook has been repeatedly criticised</a> for not doing enough to clean up its platforms, plural.</p>\n<p>Today the regulator said the social media giant has made further changes to the systems it uses for &#8220;identifying, removing and preventing the trading of fake and/or misleading reviews on its platforms to ensure it is fulfilling its previous commitments&#8221;.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s not clear why it&#8217;s taken Facebook well over a year &#8212; and a number of high profile interventions &#8212; to dial up action against the trade in fake reviews. But the company suggested that the resources it has available to tackle the problem had been strained as a result of the COVID-19 pandemic and associated impacts, such as home working. (Facebook&#8217;s <a href=\"https://investor.fb.com/investor-news/press-release-details/2021/Facebook-Reports-Fourth-Quarter-and-Full-Year-2020-Results/default.aspx\">full year revenue</a> increased in 2020 but so too did its expenses.)</p>\n<p>According to the CMA changes Facebook has made to its system for combating traders of fake reviews include:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>suspending or banning users who are repeatedly creating Facebook groups and Instagram profiles that promote, encourage or facilitate fake and misleading reviews</li>\n<li>introducing new automated processes that will improve the detection and removal of this content</li>\n<li>making it harder for people to use Facebook’s search tools to find fake and misleading review groups and profiles on Facebook and Instagram</li>\n<li>putting in place dedicated processes to make sure that these changes continue to work effectively and stop the problems from reappearing</li>\n</ul>\n<p>Again it&#8217;s not clear why Facebook would not have already been suspending or banning repeat offenders &#8212; at least, not if it was actually taking good faith action to genuinely quash the problem, rather than seeing if it could get away with doing the bare minimum.</p>\n<p>Commenting in a statement, Andrea Coscelli, chief executive of the CMA, essentially makes that point, saying: &#8220;Facebook has a duty to do all it can to stop the trading of such content on its platforms. After we intervened again, the company made significant changes &#8212; but it is disappointing it has taken them over a year to fix these issues.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;We will continue to keep a close eye on Facebook, including its Instagram business. Should we find it is failing to honour its commitments, we will not hesitate to take further action,&#8221; Coscelli added.</p>\n<p>A quick search on Facebook&#8217;s platform for UK groups trading in fake reviews appears to return fewer obviously dubious results than when we&#8217;ve checked in on this problem in <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/06/21/ebay-and-facebook-told-to-tackle-trade-in-fake-reviews/\">2019</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/08/facebook-and-ebay-pledge-to-do-more-to-tackle-trade-in-fake-reviews-after-pressure-from-uk-regulator/\">2020</a>. Although the results that were returned included a number of private groups so it was not immediately possible to verify what content is being solicited from members.</p>\n<p>We did also find a number of Facebook groups offering Amazon reviews intended for other European markets, such as France and Spain (and in one public group aimed at Amazon Spain we found someone offering a &#8220;fee&#8221; via PayPal for a review; see below screengrab) &#8212; suggesting Facebook isn&#8217;t applying the same level of attention to tackling fake reviews that are being traded by users in markets where it&#8217;s faced fewer regulatory pokes than it has in the UK.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2136423\" style=\"width: 574px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img
