+0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Screenshot-2021-04-09-at-16.31.57.png?w=564","linkMd5":"5f3a3bdbd3af9680feeef998df54598f","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn31@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-41-36-360_e77196cbd53afce8.webp","destWidth":564,"destHeight":680,"sourceBytes":102598,"destBytes":102598,"author":"Natasha Lomas","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/Screenshot-2021-04-09-at-16.31.57.png?w=564":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn31@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-41-36-360_e77196cbd53afce8.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn35@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-41-36-205_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn47@2020_5/2021/04/09/16-42-25-878_6be3d6b3141e6636.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn4@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-25-351_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=YeS_LMWKIJQ:HuqDiSlJKx8:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn9@2020_4/2021/04/09/16-42-25-329_3701230aff447954.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=YeS_LMWKIJQ:HuqDiSlJKx8:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn75@2020_1/2021/04/09/16-42-26-003_eed258ab24efed42.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn67@2020_3/2021/04/09/16-42-25-759_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/YeS_LMWKIJQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn87@2020_6/2021/04/09/16-42-25-818_7ce03f3f17ba8db3.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617986495987},{"createdTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:36","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:36","title":"Chinese hardware makers turn to crowdfunding as they look to go global","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136286","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">China&#8217;s tech giants have had a rough time in Western markets over the last few years. Huawei and DJI have been hit by trade restrictions, while TikTok and WeChat are threatened with their apps being banned in the U.S. Overall, Chinese companies with an overseas footprint are<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/09/chinese-hardware-global-expansion-geopolitics/\"> increasingly wary of rising geopolitical tensions</a>.</p>\n<p>But at an event hosted by California-based crowdfunding platform Indiegogo for Chinese consumer product makers in Shenzhen, businesses from sizes ranging from a startup making portable power stations to 53-year-old home appliances behemoth Midea, listened attentively as Indiegogo&#8217;s China managers shed light on how to court Western consumers.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The first stage is to let ourselves be heard by the world. We have done that,&#8221; Li Yongqin, general manager of Indiegogo China, exhorted a room of entrepreneurs. &#8220;Next, we will bravely ride the tide and accept the challenge of coming the brands loved by users around the world.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>For Midea, &#8220;crowdfunding gives us a very direct way to understand consumers,&#8221; said Chen Zhenrui, who oversees the group&#8217;s overseas e-commerce initiative. Platforms like Indiegogo and Kickstarter are ways for individuals and organizations to raise capital from a large number of people to fund a project. In most cases, backers get perks or rewards from the project they fund.</p>\n<p>Midea <a href=\"https://www.indiegogo.com/projects/midea-the-window-air-conditioner-reinvented#/\">raised $1.5 million</a> last year for a new air conditioner unit launched on Indiegogo, an almost negligible amount compared to the 280 billion yuan ($42 billion) annual revenue it generated in 2019. But the support from its 3,600 backers on Indiegogo was more a proof of concept.</p>\n<p>Within a few weeks, Midea learned that a compact air conditioner that saddles snugly on the window sill, blocks out noise and saves energy could entice many American consumers. Like other established Chinese home appliances makers, Midea had been exporting for several decades.</p>\n<p>But &#8220;in the past, much of our overseas business was in the traditional, B2B export realm. I think we are still far from being a world-class brand,&#8221; said Chen.</p>\n<p>When Midea first launched on Indiegogo, a user left comments on its campaign page calling the project a scam: How could a Fortune Global 500 company be on Indiegogo?</p>\n<p>&#8220;Through rounds of communication, we got to know each other. That user gave us a big push,&#8221; Chen recalled, adding that Midea used a dozen of suggestions from Indiegogo backers to improve its product.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2136299\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2136299\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2136299 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/45911617951684_.pic_hd.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"768\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/45911617951684_.pic_hd.jpg 4032w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/45911617951684_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=150,113 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/45911617951684_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=300,225 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/45911617951684_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=768,576 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/45911617951684_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=680,510 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/45911617951684_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=1536,1152 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/45911617951684_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=2048,1536 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/45911617951684_.pic_hd.jpg?resize=50,38 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2136299\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">Li Yongqin, general manager of Indiegogo China, exhorted a room of entrepreneurs to develop brands loved by global users. Photo: TechCrunch</p></div></p>\n<p>More and more traditional manufacturers from China are giving crowdfunding a shot. Padmate, based in the southern coastal city of Xiamen, built a new earbud brand called Pamu from its foundation as a white-label maker of sound systems.</p>\n<p>Edison Shen, a director at Padmate, said that traditional export was getting harder as old-school distributors became squeezed by new retail channels like e-commerce. By creating their own brands and reaching consumers directly, factories could also improve profit margins. Padmate went on Indiegogo in 2018 and raised <a href=\"https://www.indiegogo.com/projects/pamu-slide-born-for-music-never-fall-out#/\">over $6.6 million</a> in one of its wireless headphone campaigns.</p>\n<p>Most of the projects on Indiegogo will go beyond the <a href=\"https://www.indiegogo.com/about/our-story\">9-million-backer</a> crowdfunding site onto mainstream platforms, listing on Amazon as well as advertising on Google and Facebook. Though the core services of these American Big Tech firms aren&#8217;t available in China, they have all set up some form of operational presence in China, whether it&#8217;s stationing staff in the country like Amazon or working through local ad resellers like Facebook.</p>\n<p>Indiegogo itself opened its China office in Shenzhen five years ago and has since seen China-based projects raise over $300 million through its platform, according to Lu Li, general manager for Indiegogo’s global strategy. China is now the company&#8217;s fastest-growing market and accounted for over 40% of the campaigns that raised over $1 million in 2020.</p>\n<p>Kickstarter, a rival to Indiegogo, also saw a surge in projects from China, which reached a <a href=\"https://mp.weixin.qq.com/s/dLvvZ_AnMvamxS6AjjCi8A\">record $60.5 million</a> in funding in 2020. The Brooklyn-based company recently began looking for a <a href=\"https://jobs.lever.co/kickstarter/e4027911-54dd-4549-aacb-f7404f3d1665\">contractor</a> in Shenzhen or the adjacent city Hong Kong to help it research the Chinese market.</p>\n<p>&#8220;In recent years, more Chinese companies are getting the hang of crowdfunding and taking their brand global, so &#8216;blockbuster&#8217; campaigns [from China] are also on the rise,&#8221; observed Li.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"eHh9lTj29X\"><p><a 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"Cleo Capital is targeting $20 million for Fund II","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136135","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a href=\"https://www.cleocap.com/\">Cleo Capital</a>, a venture capital firm founded in 2018 by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/sarahkunst\">Sarah Kunst</a>, is raising up to $20 million for its second fund, according to a source familiar with the matter. <a href=\"https://www.sec.gov/Archives/edgar/data/1855059/000185505921000001/xslFormDX01/primary_doc.xml\">A recent SEC filing</a> shows that Cleo Capital has already raised $6.7 million of that goal, bringing total assets under management to around $10 million. Kunst was unable to comment on her fundraising efforts.</p>\n<p>That new AUM number is close to what Cleo Capital initially set out to do. When Kunst first launched her firm, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/08/28/cleo-capital-sets-10m-target-to-fund-female-entrepreneurs/\">she targeted a $10 million close.</a> She ended up closing $3.14 million of that goal, and now, she’s back to double down.</p>\n<p>Fund II’s $20 million target, if closed, would allow Cleo Capital, which invests in primarily pre-seed companies, to start leading rounds. The firm has already been writing $1 million checks and targets about a 15-20% ownership in its rounds.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>“One of the reasons why we are a pre-seed fund is because in seed, especially late-seed, you have everyone from family offices to TikTok stars and rolling funds competing for hot rounds,” she said. “No one is competing in pre-seed.”</p>\n<p>There are firms such as Precursor and Hustle Fund that back pre-seed companies, and cut checks around $100,000 and $25,000 to start, respectively. Kunst sees the ability to write a $1 million pre-seed check as a “huge advantage.” Usually early-stage founders without family money or deep networks have to spend a big chunk of time raising their first round. It’s a lot of time to spend fundraising and not building a company. If a firm can cut a big pre-seed check, she thinks that Cleo is “buying back six months of a company‘s runway,” she said.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/11/as-covid-19-era-drags-on-vcs-look-beyond-zoom-calls-for-due-diligence-and-sourcing/\">Like many firms</a>, Cleo Capital has turned to creative measures to diversify deal flow in the era of Zoom investing and pandemic business. For example, Cleo Capital<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/28/cleo-capitals-sarah-kunst-launches-a-fellowship-for-laid-off-workers/\"> launched a fellowship program</a> for laid off workers during COVID-19 to promote entrepreneurship.</p>\n<p>Matt Pauker, a repeat founder who has sold companies to Coinbase and HP Enterprise, was one of the advisors of that program. Pauker has joined Cleo Capital as a general partner presumably to line up with the timing of Fund II.</p>\n<p>While the firm has no racial or gender investment focus, about 92% of its current investments are companies started by underrepresented founders.</p>\n<p>The firm’s portfolio includes Planet FWD, mmhmm, Lunch Club, and StyleSeat. As for new opportunities, Kunst says that Cleo Capital is looking at anything that helps the individual turn into a collective. With the growth of the creator economy and solo-entrepreneurs, people need to figure out the future of income, health care, and benefit, Kunst explained.</p>\n<p>“All of these things are hard for people to do as an individual,” she said. The majority of Cleo Capital’s portfolio is based outside of Silicon Valley.</p>\n<p>Cleo Capital&#8217;s raise comes just over a week after two venture capital firms founded by Black venture capitalists announced new funds, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/31/harlem-capital-fund-ii/\">Harlem Capital</a> and <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/25/closing-on-103-million-mac-venture-capital-is-changing-the-face-of-venture-capital/\">MaC Venture Capital.</a></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote id=\"speakable-summary\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Digital mortgage lender Better.com has raised a $500 million round from Japanese investment conglomerate SoftBank that values the company at $6 billion.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The financing is notable for a few reasons. For one, that new $6 billion valuation,  is up 50% from the $4 billion it was valued at last November when it raised $200 million in Series D financing. It’s also up tenfold from its $600 million valuation at the time of its </span><a href=\"https://news.crunchbase.com/news/better-com-raises-160m-series-c-at-600m-valuation-to-speed-up-mortgage-lending/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Series C raise</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> in August 2019.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Secondly, it’s further proof that mortgage – a traditionally “unsexy” industry that has long been in need of disruption – is officially hot. For all its controversy, when SoftBank invests, people pay attention.</span></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The COVID-19 pandemic and historically-low mortgage rates fueled acceleration in the online lending space in a way that no one could have anticipated. That, combined with the general fervour in venture funding, means it’s not a big surprise that Better.com has raised $700 million in just a matter of months.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The investment brings Better.com’s total funding raised to over $900 million since its 2014 inception. Other backers include Goldman Sachs, Kleiner Perkins, American Express, Activant Capital and Citi, among others.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to the <a href=\"https://www.wsj.com/articles/softbank-to-invest-500-million-in-mortgage-startup-better-11617899907\">Wall Street Journal</a>, </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">SoftBank is buying shares from Better’s existing investors, and agreed to give all of its voting rights to CEO and founder Vishal Garg “in a sign of its eagerness” to invest in the company. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">During a one-on-one interview at Lendit Fintech’s USA 2020 virtual event in October, Garg had told me that an IPO was definitely in the works.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“We’ll do it when it’s right,” he said. “One of the core tenets of American capitalism is the ability for your customers to buy your stock.”</span></p>\n<p>And in February, Bloomberg had reported that the startup had  tapped Morgan Stanley and Bank of America Corp. for a planned initial public offering in the U.S. But there&#8217;s been no further word since. It&#8217;s not unusual for companies to raise large sums before an IPO. Affirm did it <a href=\"https://finledger.com/2020/11/18/affirm-drops-s-1-revealing-sharply-rising-revenue-on-a-narrower-net-loss/\">last year</a>, for example.</p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Also last October, Varg had told me that before the pandemic, Better was processing about $1.2 billion a month in loans. But as of October 2020, it was funding over $2.5 billion per month, and had gone from 1,500 staffers to about 4,000 worldwide. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">“When the pandemic started we were doing less than sort of like $50 million a month of revenue,” he said at the time. “We’re two-and-a half times that now.”</span></p>\n<p>Since then, those numbers have gone up even more. A company spokesperson told me today that Better.com funded $14 billion in loan volume in the first quarter of 2021 alone and that it is currently funding over $4 billions in loans a month. For some context,  Better.com funded $25 billion in loan volume in all of 2020. And, it currently has 6,000 employees – up 2,000 from last October.</p>\n<p><em>This article was updated post-publication with some additional numbers provided by the company.</em></p>\n<div in-house techies to configure software on behalf of other staff, access to the most powerful tech tools &#8212; at the &#8216;deep tech&#8217; AI coal face &#8212; still requires some expert help (and/or costly in-house expertise).</p>\n<p>This is where bootstrapping French startup, <a href=\"https://nlpcloud.io\">NLPCloud.io</a>, is plying a trade in MLOps/AIOps &#8212; or &#8216;compute intelligence have, in recent years, led to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/02/17/openai-text-generator-dangerous/\">impressive advances in the field of NLP</a> &#8212; a technology that can help businesses scale their capacity to intelligently grapple with all sorts of communications by automating tasks like Named Entity Recognition, sentiment-analysis, text classification, summarization, question answering, and Part-Of-Speech tagging, freeing up (human) staff to focus on more complex/nuanced work. (Although it&#8217;s worth emphasizing that the bulk of NLP research has focused on the English language &#8212; meaning that&#8217;s where this tech is most mature; so associated AI advances are not universally distributed.)</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"78mJtCyFNR\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/02/17/openai-text-generator-dangerous/\">OpenAI built a text generator so good, it&#8217;s considered too dangerous to release</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;OpenAI built a text generator so good, it&#8217;s considered too dangerous to release&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/02/17/openai-text-generator-dangerous/embed/#?secret=78mJtCyFNR\" data-secret=\"78mJtCyFNR\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Production ready (pre-trained) NLP models for English are readily available &#8216;out of the box&#8217;. There are also dedicated open source frameworks offering help with training models. But businesses wanting to tap into NLP still need to have the DevOps resource and chops to implement NLP models.</p>\n<p>NLPCloud.io is catering to businesses that don&#8217;t feel up to the implementation challenge themselves &#8212; offering &#8220;production-ready NLP API&#8221; with the promise of &#8220;no DevOps required&#8221;.</p>\n<p>Its API is based on <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/11/hugging-face-raises-40-million-for-its-natural-language-processing-library/\">Hugging Face</a> and <a href=\"https://spacy.io\">spaCy</a> open-source models. Customers can either choose to use ready-to-use pre-trained models (it selects the &#8220;best&#8221; open source models; it does not build its own); or they can upload custom models developed internally by their own data scientists &#8212; which it says is a point of differentiation vs SaaS services such as Google Natural Language (which uses Google&#8217;s ML models) or Amazon Comprehend and Monkey Learn.</p>\n<p>NLPCloud.io says it wants to democratize NLP by helping developers and data scientists deliver these projects &#8220;in no time and at a fair price&#8221;. (It has a tiered <a href=\"https://nlpcloud.io/#plans\">pricing model</a> based on requests per minute, which starts at $39pm and ranges up to $1,199pm, at the enterprise end, for one custom model running on a GPU. It does also offer a free tier so users can test models at low request velocity without incurring a charge.)</p>\n<p>&#8220;The idea came from the fact that, as a software engineer, I saw many AI projects fail because of the deployment to production phase,&#8221; says sole founder and CTO Julien Salinas. &#8220;Companies often focus on building accurate and fast AI models but today more and more excellent open-source models are available and are doing an excellent job&#8230; so the toughest challenge now is being able to efficiently use these models in production. It takes AI skills, DevOps skills, programming skill&#8230; which is why it&#8217;s a challenge for so many companies, and which is why I decided to launch NLPCloud.io.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The platform launched in January 2021 and now has around 500 users, including 30 who are paying for the service. While the startup, which is based in Grenoble, in the French Alps, is a team of three for now, plus a couple of independent contractors. (Salinas says he plans to hire five people by the end of the year.)</p>\n<p>&#8220;Most of our users are tech startups but we also start having a couple of bigger companies,&#8221; he tells TechCrunch. &#8220;The biggest demand I&#8217;m seeing is both from software engineers and data scientists. Sometimes it&#8217;s from teams who have data science skills but don&#8217;t have DevOps skills (or don&#8217;t want to spend time on this). Sometimes it&#8217;s from tech teams who want to leverage NLP out-of-the-box without hiring a whole data science team.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;We have very diverse customers, from solo startup founders to bigger companies like BBVA, Mintel, Senuto&#8230; in all sorts of sectors (banking, public relations, market research),&#8221; he adds.</p>\n<p>Use cases of its customers include lead generation from unstructured text (such as web pages), via named entities extraction; and sorting support tickets based on urgency by conducting sentiment analysis.</p>\n<p>Content marketers are also using its platform for headline generation (via summarization). While text classification capabilities are being used for economic intelligence and financial data extraction, per Salinas.</p>\n<p>He says his own experience as a CTO and software engineer working on NLP projects at a number of tech companies led him to spot an opportunity in the challenge of AI implementation.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I realized that it was quite easy to build acceptable NLP models thanks to great open-source frameworks like spaCy and Hugging Face Transformers but then I found it quite hard to use these models in production,&#8221; he explains. &#8220;It takes programming skills in order to develop an API, strong DevOps skills in order to build a robust and fast infrastructure to serve NLP models (AI models in general consume a lot of resources), and also data science skills of course.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I tried to look for ready-to-use cloud solutions in order to save weeks of work but I couldn&#8217;t find anything satisfactory. My intuition was that such a platform would help tech teams save a lot of time, sometimes months of work for the teams who don&#8217;t have strong DevOps profiles.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;NLP has been around for decades but until recently it took whole teams of data scientists to build acceptable NLP models. For a couple of years, we&#8217;ve made amazing progress in terms of accuracy and speed of the NLP models. More and more experts who have been working in the NLP field for decades agree that NLP is becoming a &#8216;commodity&#8217;,&#8221; he goes on. &#8220;Frameworks like spaCy make it extremely simple for developers to leverage NLP models without having advanced data science knowledge. And Hugging Face&#8217;s open-source repository for NLP models is also a great step in this direction.</p>\n<p>&#8220;But having these models run in production is still hard, and maybe even harder than before as these brand new models are very demanding in terms of resources.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The models NLPCloud.io offers are picked for performance &#8212; where &#8220;best&#8221; means it has &#8220;the best compromise between accuracy and speed&#8221;. Salinas also says they are paying mind to context, given NLP can be used for diverse user cases &#8212; hence proposing number of models so as to be able to adapt to a given use.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Initially we started with models dedicated to entities extraction only but most of our first customers also asked for other use cases too, so we started adding other models,&#8221; he notes, adding that they will continue to add more models from the two chosen frameworks &#8212; &#8220;in order to cover more use cases, and more languages&#8221;.</p>\n<p>SpaCy and Hugging Face, meanwhile, were chosen to be the source for the models offered via its API based on their track record as companies, the NLP libraries they offer and their focus on production-ready framework &#8212; with the combination allowing NLPCloud.io to offer a selection of models that are fast and accurate, working within the bounds of respective trade-offs, according to Salinas.</p>\n<p>&#8220;SpaCy is developed by a solid company in Germany called Explosion.ai. This library has become one of the most used NLP libraries among companies who want to leverage NLP in production &#8216;for real&#8217; (as opposed to academic research only). The reason is that it is very fast, has great accuracy in most scenarios, and is an opinionated&#8221; framework which makes it very simple to use by non-data scientists (the tradeoff is that it gives less customization possibilities),&#8221; he says.</p>\n<p>&#8220;<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/12/17/hugging-face-raises-15-million-to-build-the-definitive-natural-language-processing-library/\">Hugging Face</a> is an even more solid company that <a title=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/11/hugging-face-raises-40-million-for-its-natural-language-processing-library/\" href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/11/hugging-face-raises-40-million-for-its-natural-language-processing-library/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\" data-saferedirecturl=\"https://www.google.com/url?q=https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/11/hugging-face-raises-40-million-for-its-natural-language-processing-library/&#38;source=gmail&#38;ust=1618050204207000&#38;usg=AFQjCNEmZDvxn9bG1Q7PE1ap2fYv2iJmDw\">recently raised $40M</a> for a good reason: They created a disruptive NLP library called &#8216;transformers&#8217; that improves a lot the accuracy of NLP models (the tradeoff is that it is very resource intensive though). It gives the opportunity to cover more use cases like sentiment analysis, classification, summarization&#8230; In addition to that, they created an open-source repository where it is easy to select the best model you need for your use case.&#8221;</p>\n<p>While AI is advancing at a clip within certain tracks &#8212; such as NLP for English &#8212; there are still caveats and potential pitfalls attached to automating language processing and analysis, with the risk of getting stuff wrong or worse. AI models trained on human-generated data have, for example, been shown reflecting embedded biases and prejudices of the people who produced the underlying data.</p>\n<p>Salinas agrees NLP can sometimes face &#8220;concerning bias issues&#8221;, such as racism and misogyny. But he expresses confidence in the models they&#8217;ve selected.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Most of the time it seems [bias in NLP] is due to the underlying data used to trained the models. It shows we should be more careful about the origin of this data,&#8221; he says. &#8220;In my opinion the best solution in order to mitigate this is that the community of NLP users should actively report something inappropriate when using a specific model so that this model can be paused and fixed.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;Even if we doubt that such a bias exists in the models we&#8217;re proposing, we do encourage our users to report such problems to us so we can take measures,&#8221; he adds.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"8Cronl3VfE\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/11/hugging-face-raises-40-million-for-its-natural-language-processing-library/\">Hugging Face raises $40 million for its natural 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"Watch a monkey equipped with Elon Musk’s Neuralink device play Pong with its brain","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136271","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><iframe class='youtube-player' width='640' height='360' src='https://www.youtube.com/embed/rsCul1sp4hQ?version=3&#038;rel=1&#038;showsearch=0&#038;showinfo=1&#038;iv_load_policy=1&#038;fs=1&#038;hl=en-US&#038;autohide=2&#038;wmode=transparent' allowfullscreen='true' style='border:0;' sandbox='allow-scripts allow-same-origin allow-popups allow-presentation'></iframe></p>\n<p>Elon Musk&#8217;s Neuralink, one of his many companies and the only one currently focused on mind control (that we&#8217;re aware of), has <a href=\"https://neuralink.com/blog/\">released a new blog post</a> and video detailing some of its recent updates — including using its hardware to make it possible for a monkey to play pong with only its brain.</p>\n<p>In the video above, Neuralink demonstrates how it used its sensor hardware and brain implant to record a baseline of activity from this macaque (named &#8216;Pager&#8217;) as it played a game on-screen where it had to move a token to different squares using a joystick with its hand. Using that baseline data, Neuralink was able to use machine learning to anticipate where Pager was going to be moving the physical controller, and was eventually able to predict it accurately before the move was actually made. Researchers then removed the paddle entirely, and eventually did the same thing with Pong, ultimately ending up at a place where Pager no longer was even moving its hand on the air on the nonexistent paddle, and was instead controlling the in-game action entirely with its mind via the Link hardware and embedded neural threads.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>\t<div class=\"article-block block--callout block--right\" >\n\t\t<h4 class=\"block--callout__title\">Read more on TechCrunch</h4>\n\t\t\n<ul>\n<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/04/16/greg-epstein-douglas-rushkoff-team-human-interview/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Douglas Rushkoff on ‘Team Human’ and fighting for our place in the future</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/28/deep-science-robot-perception-acoustic-monitoring-using-ml-to-detect-arthritis/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Deep Science: Robot perception, acoustic monitoring, using ML to detect arthritis</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/28/take-a-closer-look-at-elon-musks-neuralink-surgical-robot/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Take a closer look at Elon Musk’s Neuralink surgical robot</a></li>\n<li><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2017/03/27/elon-musks-neuralink-wants-to-boost-the-brain-to-keep-up-with-ai/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Elon Musk’s Neuralink wants to boost the brain to keep up with AI</a></li>\n</ul>\n\t</div>\n\t</p>\n<p>The last we saw of Neuralink, Musk himself was demonstrating the Link tech live in August 2020, using pigs to show how it was able to read signals from the brain depending on different stimuli. This new demo with Pager more clearly outlines the direction that the tech is headed in terms of human applications, since, as the company shared on its blog, the same technology could be used to help patients with paralysis manipulate a cursor on a computer, for instance. That could be applied to other paradigms as well, including touch controls on an iPhone, and even typing using a virtual keyboard, according to the company.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"QPozEqp3Hd\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/28/elon-musk-demonstrates-neuralinks-tech-live-using-pigs-with-surgically-implanted-brain-monitoring-devices/\">Elon Musk demonstrates Neuralink&#8217;s tech live using pigs with surgically implanted brain-monitoring devices</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Elon Musk demonstrates Neuralink&#8217;s tech live using pigs with surgically implanted brain-monitoring devices&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/28/elon-musk-demonstrates-neuralinks-tech-live-using-pigs-with-surgically-implanted-brain-monitoring-devices/embed/#?secret=QPozEqp3Hd\" data-secret=\"QPozEqp3Hd\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Musk separately tweeted that in fact, he expects the initial version of Neuralink&#8217;s product to be able to allow someone with paralysis that prevents standard modes of phone interaction to use one faster than people using their thumbs for input. He also added that future iterations of the product would be able to enable communication between Neuralinks in different parts of a patient&#8217;s body, transmitting between an in-brain node and neural pathways in legs, for instance, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/elonmusk/status/1380316949087854595\">making it possible for &#8220;paraplegics to walk again.&#8221;</a></p>\n<p>These are obviously bold claims, but the company cites a lot of existing research that undergirds its existing demonstrations and near-term goals. Musk&#8217;s more ambitious claims, should, like all of his projections, definitely be taken with a healthy dose of skepticism. He did add that he hopes human trials will begin to get underway &#8220;hopefully later this year,&#8221; for instance – which is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/07/16/elon-musks-neuralink-looks-to-begin-outfitting-human-brains-with-faster-input-and-output-starting-next-year/\">already two years later than he was initially anticipating those might start</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"QMrSInt0q5\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/07/16/elon-musks-neuralink-looks-to-begin-outfitting-human-brains-with-faster-input-and-output-starting-next-year/\">Elon Musk&#8217;s Neuralink looks to begin outfitting human brains with faster input and output starting next year</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" id=\"speakable-summary\">It’s been a little over a week since union voting concluded for Amazon warehouse workers in Bessemer, Alabama. Things have been fairly quiet in the eye of the storm for most of it. That changed today, however, as vote counting began in earnest. Thus far, things are breaking pretty dramatically in the company’s favor, following a hard-fought <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/26/amazon-goes-on-the-offensive-ahead-of-next-weeks-union-vote-counting/\">anti-union campaign</a>.</p>\n<p>As of the end of the day, <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/technology/2021/04/08/amazon-bessemer-mailbox-union/\">no votes have more than doubled</a> the yeses, at 1,100 to 463. With counting resuming &#8212; and likely concluding &#8212; tomorrow, the Retail, Wholesale and Department Store Union, which would potentially serve as the worker’s union, is decrying the company’s tactics.</p>\n<p>“Our system is broken, Amazon took full advantage of that, and we will be calling on the labor board to hold Amazon accountable for its illegal and egregious behavior during the campaign,” RWDSU President Stuart Appelbaum said in a statement provided to TechCrunch. “But make no mistake about it; this still represents an important moment for working people and their voices will be heard.”</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The comments appear to be as much about actions the company has taken during the campaign as it is bracing for a likely challenge to the results. The numbers constitute around half of the 3,215 ballots that are being counted. They put Amazon around 500 no votes away from defeating union efforts.</p>\n<p>We have reached out to the company for a response to Appelbaum’s comment, but have not heard back. In a comment offered to TechCrunch last month, the company had less than stellar words about Appelbaum, calling the union head the “Chief Disinformation Officer,” adding that “in an attempt to save his long declining union, [he] is taking alternative facts to a whole new level.”</p>\n<p>Regardless of the final count, this process is likely to be drawn out. Among the complaints are reports that the company pushed the USPS to install an illegal ballot box, breaking National Labor Relations Board rulings in the process.</p>\n<div class=\"embed 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"Facebook ran ads for a fake ‘Clubhouse for PC’ app planted with malware","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136151","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Cybercriminals have taken out a number of Facebook ads masquerading as a Clubhouse app for PC users in order to target unsuspecting victims with malware, TechCrunch has learned.</p>\n<p>TechCrunch was alerted Wednesday to Facebook ads tied to several Facebook pages impersonating Clubhouse, the drop-in audio chat app only available on iPhones. Clicking on the ad would open a fake Clubhouse website, including a mocked-up screenshot of what the non-existent PC app looks like, with a download link to the malicious app.</p>\n<p>When opened, the malicious app tries to communicate with a command and control server to obtain instructions on what to do next. One <a href=\"https://www.vmray.com/analyses/acc6e8793536/report/overview.html\">sandbox analysis of the malware</a> showed the malicious app tried to infect the isolated machine with ransomware.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>But overnight, the fake Clubhouse websites — which were hosted in Russia — went offline. In doing so, the malware also stopped working. Guardicore&#8217;s Amit Serper, who tested the malware in a sandbox on Thursday, said the malware received an error from the server and did nothing more.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2136198\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2136198\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2136198 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/fake-clubhouse-website-highres.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"1103\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/fake-clubhouse-website-highres.jpg 1380w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/fake-clubhouse-website-highres.jpg?resize=139,150 139w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/fake-clubhouse-website-highres.jpg?resize=279,300 279w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/fake-clubhouse-website-highres.jpg?resize=768,827 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/fake-clubhouse-website-highres.jpg?resize=631,680 631w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/fake-clubhouse-website-highres.jpg?resize=46,50 46w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1024px) 100vw, 1024px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2136198\" class=\"wp-caption-text\">The fake website was set up to look like Clubhouse&#8217;s real website, but featuring a malicious PC app. (Image: TechCrunch)</p></div></p>\n<p>It&#8217;s not uncommon for cybercriminals to tailor their malware campaigns to piggyback off the successes of wildly popular apps. Clubhouse reportedly topped <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/02/18/report-social-audio-app-clubhouse-has-topped-8-million-global-downloads/\">more than 8 million global downloads to date</a> despite an invite-only launch. That high demand prompted a scramble to reverse-engineer the app to <a href=\"https://www.vice.com/en/article/y3gj5j/android-version-clubhouse\">build bootleg versions</a> of it to evade Clubhouse&#8217;s gated walls, but also <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/02/22/clubhouse-security/\">government censors</a> where the app is blocked.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"RSW9wBrwKW\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/26/android-malware-system-update/\">A new Android spyware masquerades as a &#8216;system update&#8217;</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;A new Android spyware masquerades as a &#8216;system update&#8217;&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/26/android-malware-system-update/embed/#?secret=RSW9wBrwKW\" data-secret=\"RSW9wBrwKW\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Each of the Facebook pages impersonating Clubhouse only had a handful of likes, but were still active at the time of publication. When reached, Facebook wouldn&#8217;t say how many account owners had clicked on the ads pointing to the fake Clubhouse websites.</p>\n<p>At least nine ads were placed this week between Tuesday and Thursday. Several of the ads said Clubhouse &#8220;is now available for PC,&#8221; while another featured a photo of co-founders Paul Davidson and Rohan Seth. Clubhouse did not return a request for comment.</p>\n<p>The ads have been removed from <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/26/facebooks-latest-ad-tool-fail-puts-another-dent-in-its-reputation/\">Facebook&#8217;s Ad Library</a>, but we have <a href=\"https://www.documentcloud.org/documents/20606747-facebook-serving-malicious-ads\">published a copy</a>. It&#8217;s also not clear how the ads made it through Facebook&#8217;s processes in the first place.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"7Y6K3N4C6j\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2021/03/13/why-blaming-the-intern-wont-save-startups-from-cybersecurity-liability/\">Why &#8216;blaming the intern&#8217; won&#8217;t 00:41:35","updatedTime":"2021-04-10 00:41:35","title":"Vybe raises $2.9 million for its challenger bank for teens","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2136340","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">French startup <a href=\"https://vybecard.com\">Vybe</a> has raised a $2.9 million funding round (€2.4 million) to build a challenger bank for teens. The company is currently testing its product with a soft launch. Users get a Mastercard payment card paired with an e-wallet.</p>\n<p>Each Vybe account comes with its own IBAN so that users can send and receive money. If you want to open an account and you are less than 18 years old, you have to go through the KYC process (know your identity) with your parent.</p>\n<p>As for parents, they can set up some limits on card payments or even block the card. Parents can also view transactions. The startup plans to generate revenue from interchange fees as well as partnership with brands and a reward system.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>While Vybe isn’t technically live, the company has attracted 375,000 downloads. Overall, 260,000 teens have pre-ordered a card already. Thousands of cards have been delivered and the first metrics are encouraging. Early adopters tend to use their card once every two days.</p>\n<p>Today’s fund is a round extension from existing investors. Investors include Ronan Le Moal, the former CEO of Crédit Mutuel Arkéa, Kick Club and Manoel Amorim.</p>\n<p>Banking products for teenagers are a lucrative segment. In France, there are several companies trying to position themselves on this segment, such as <a href=\"https://www.kard.eu\">Kard</a>, <a href=\"https://www.pixpay.fr\">PixPay</a> and <a href=\"https://www.xaalys.com\">Xaalys</a>. Most of these companies charge a subscription fee to access the service.</p>\n<p>Other fintech companies that aren’t specifically targeting young people could also work well with teenagers. For instance, young users can open a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/17/revolut-launches-revolut-junior-to-help-you-manage-allowance/\">Revolut Junior</a> or <a href=\"https://lydia-app.com\">Lydia</a> account and receive money from their parents.</p>\n<p>In the U.S., startups offering debit cards for children are about to reach unicorn status. As The Information’s Kate Clark <a href=\"https://www.theinformation.com/articles/kid-debit-card-startup-greenlight-valued-at-2-billion-in-andreessen-led-round\">reported</a>, <a href=\"https://www.greenlightcard.com\">Greenlight</a>, <a href=\"https://current.com\">Current</a> and <a href=\"https://www.step.com\">Step</a> are all raising new funding rounds with a valuation between $1 billion and $2 billion.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2136341\" style=\"width: 1034px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2136341\" loading=\"lazy\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2021/04/phoneCard.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"1024\" height=\"1504\" class=\"vertical size-full wp-image-2136341\"
